If there are many streams\n715:   // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. complicated, but important.\n1312: //\n1313: // We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter\n1314: // chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,\n1315: // e.g. registering access logging.\n1316: //\n1317: // This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one\n1318: // can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to\n1319: // serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and\n1320: // modifications which may themselves affect route selection.\n1321: void The most significant gaps involve deferred request processing under load, zombie stream lifecycle management, premature stream reset detection, complex gRPC timeout calculation, and HTTP/1-specific soft drain behavior. These gaps could allow subtle bugs in request buffering, stream cleanup, connection draining, and timeout handling to slip through.\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Deferred Request Processing with Max Requests Per I/O Cycle\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~505-557, ~1566-1575\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The code implements request deferral when max requests per I/O cycle is exceeded (controlled by runtime key `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle`). When this limit is reached, requests are buffered in `deferred_data_` instead of being processed immediately. The `onDeferredRequestProcessing()` callback must later process this buffered data. The interaction between deferral, deferred data buffering, and deferred metadata handling is complex and the edge cases around buffer management during deferral are untested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `DeferredRequestProcessingMaxRequestsPerIoCycle`\n  - Setup: Configure HCM with small `max_requests_per_io_cycle` value (e.g., 2)\n  - Scenario: Send 5 rapid requests in single onData call\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify first 2 requests are processed immediately\n    - Verify requests 3-5 are buffered in deferred_data_\n    - Verify deferred requests are processed via scheduled callback\n    - Verify request ordering is preserved\n    - Verify stats: `downstream_rq_deferred_*` counters increment\n\n- **Why It Matters**: If deferral logic fails, requests could be reordered, lost, or cause buffer corruption under high load. This is a critical backpressure mechanism.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Zombie Stream Cleanup with Codec Encode Complete\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~2137-2159, ~321-392\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: When `doEndStream()` is called before response encoding completes, the stream transitions to \"zombie\" state (`state_.is_zombie_stream_ = true`). The cleanup is deferred until `onCodecEncodeComplete()` fires. The complex interaction between zombie stream creation, deferred stream destruction, and connection closure (especially the `close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete_` runtime flag) is poorly tested. There's also interaction with `shouldSkipDeferredCloseDelay()` that may not be covered.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ZombieStreamCleanupWithConnectionDrain`\n  - Setup: Enable `envoy.reloadable_features.http1_close_connection_on_zombie_stream_complete`\n  - Scenario: Trigger stream completion before response encoding finishes (e.g., via internal redirect), then simulate codec encode complete\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify zombie stream state is set\n    - Verify `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` is called on encode complete\n    - Verify deferred close check is invoked with correct skip_delay value\n    - Verify zombie stream doesn't block connection closure\n    - Verify stream timers are properly disabled\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Zombie streams can leak resources or block connection draining if cleanup fails. This affects HTTP/1.1 connection reuse and orderly shutdown.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Premature Reset Detection with Connection Draining\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~677-749\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The `isPrematureRstStream()` and `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` functions implement sophisticated logic to detect when too many streams reset prematurely (before receiving response) and drain the connection to prevent cascading failures. The logic has multiple thresholds:\n  - Per-stream lifetime check (minimum lifetime seconds)\n  - Total stream count threshold\n  - Ratio check (premature_count * 2 >= total_count)\n\n  The interaction between these thresholds and the recursion prevention flag is complex and untested. Edge cases around the ratio calculations when streams count is low are likely untested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureResetDetectionThresholdEdgeCases`\n  - Setup: Configure premature reset thresholds via runtime keys\n  - Scenarios:\n    1. Reset streams below min_lifetime threshold - should not count as premature\n    2. Multiple resets with ratio exactly at threshold boundary (50%)\n    3. Verify recursion prevention flag blocks nested calls\n    4. Verify stats: `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` incremented\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify connection drained when threshold exceeded\n    - Verify stream lifetime comparison works correctly\n    - Verify ratio calculation edge cases\n    - Verify connection close details set correctly\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Flawed premature reset detection could cause false positives (draining healthy connections) or false negatives (not detecting attack patterns). Recursion handling is critical to prevent stack overflow.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: HTTP/1 Soft Drain on Connection Duration Timeout\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~769-788\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: When `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` fires, the code has special handling for HTTP/1 if `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is configured. Instead of starting drain sequence immediately, it sets `soft_drain_http1_ = true`, which causes new streams to set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` instead of closing the connection. This ensures in-flight requests complete before closing. However, this interaction with new stream creation and the drain state machine is untested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HTTP1SoftDrainOnConnectionDurationTimeout`\n  - Setup: Configure max connection duration with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration=true`\n  - Scenario:\n    1. Establish HTTP/1.1 connection\n    2. Start long-running request\n    3. Let connection duration timeout fire while request in flight\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify soft_drain_http1_ flag is set\n    - Verify new streams after timeout get shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()\n    - Verify in-flight request completes before drain\n    - Verify stats: `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` incremented\n    - Verify no GOAWAY sent (unlike HTTP/2)\n    - Verify connection closes after current request ends\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Failed soft drain could cause HTTP/1 requests to be abruptly terminated despite the configuration intent. This affects connection lifecycle and request completion guarantees.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Complex gRPC Timeout Header Calculation with Offsets\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~1690-1776\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The `refreshDurationTimeout()` function implements sophisticated timeout logic for gRPC requests:\n  1. If no gRPC timeout header, use stream duration from route config or HCM config\n  2. If gRPC timeout header exists and route has `grpcTimeoutHeaderMax()`:\n     - Cap timeout to max value (if max != 0)\n     - Apply offset subtraction if configured\n     - Handle edge case where offset >= timeout (set to 0)\n  3. Adjust timeout based on elapsed time\n\n  The interaction between these conditions with various combinations of headers, route config, and offsets is untested. The edge case handling (offset >= timeout becoming 0) may have boundary issues.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `GrpcTimeoutHeaderCalculationEdgeCases`\n  - Scenarios:\n    1. gRPC timeout with offset exactly equal to timeout value (should become 0ms)\n    2. gRPC timeout with offset greater than timeout (should become 0ms, not negative)\n    3. gRPC max timeout set to 0 (should be ignored, no cap applied)\n    4. Multiple timeouts: grpc header > route max (should be capped)\n    5. Elapsed time causes timeout to become 0 during calculation\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify timeout never becomes negative\n    - Verify offset application doesn't exceed timeout\n    - Verify 0 timeout cap is handled correctly\n    - Verify header is rewritten with calculated value\n    - Verify timer is enabled/disabled correctly\n\n- **Why It Matters**: gRPC timeout calculation errors could cause requests to timeout prematurely or have excessively long timeouts, affecting reliability of request processing.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: Deferred Metadata Handling with Request Deferral\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~1647-1658, ~2546-2565\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: When requests are deferred (via `state_.deferred_to_next_io_iteration_`), metadata frames are pushed onto a queue (`deferred_metadata_`) instead of being processed immediately. The queue is then drained when deferred request processing occurs. However, the interaction between deferred metadata and deferred data/trailers, along with metadata ordering guarantees, is untested. There's potential for metadata to be processed out of order relative to headers/data/trailers.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `DeferredMetadataWithDeferredRequest`\n  - Setup: Configure HCM with max_requests_per_io_cycle limit\n  - Scenario:\n    1. Send request that gets deferred due to I/O cycle limit\n    2. Intersperse metadata frames between data and trailers\n    3. Verify metadata queue ordering\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify metadata queued in `deferred_metadata_` when deferred\n    - Verify deferred metadata processed after headers but before data if sent before data\n    - Verify metadata ordering relative to other frame types\n    - Verify metadata not dropped during deferral\n    - Verify stats: metadata frame counts correct\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Out-of-order metadata could cause filter logic to fail if it assumes certain metadata ordering. This could break custom protocol extensions that rely on metadata sequencing.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 7: Header Validation with UHV Mode and Error Handling\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: ~1197-1250, ~1460-1487\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The header validation logic has two paths:\n  1. Pre-UHV mode: Limited validation, specific error handling in comments\n  2. When this limit is reached, requests are buffered in `deferred_data_` instead of being processed immediately. The `onDeferredRequestProcessing()` callback must later process this buffered data.
